Jin Guobao's Talk After Returning Home 26

Details of the Investigation in Japan

Population Survey of Six Major Cities

Uniformity of Municipal Finance

A Glimpse of Japan's National Transformation

Jin Guobao, the former Director of the Beijing Municipal Finance Bureau, was dispatched to Japan by the Municipal Government to investigate municipal finance. He has already returned to Beijing. Commissioner Jin is now organizing and researching what he learned in Japan, which will take about ten days to complete. He will then contribute it to the government for adoption as a reference for reforming our country's municipal finance. Yesterday, a reporter from the Daily News visited Mr. Jin at his private residence to ask about the results of his investigation. He told the reporter in great detail, and the following is a summary:

Population Survey: After I was dispatched to Japan to investigate municipal finance, I was warmly received by the municipal governments of various places. Since the earthquake in Japan, it has been striving to restore its construction business, which is beyond the reach of ordinary people. There are six major cities in the country: (1) Tokyo, (2) Osaka, (3) Kyoto (i.e., Xijing), (4) Kobe, (5) Nagoya, and (6) Yokohama. The government that manages municipal affairs in Japan is called the city office, which is directly under the prefecture government. This is the difference between it and our country's city status. However, the selection of the mayor is completely civilian and is not appointed by the government. The mayor is elected by all the citizens of the city. Therefore, the mayor's prestige and talent often surpass those of the prefectural governor, so the city's administrative scope is also quite broad. The estimated population of the six major cities recently is as follows: (1) Tokyo 2,218,400, (2) Osaka 2,333,800, (3) Nagoya 949,966, (4) Kyoto 736,000, (5) Kobe 717,771, and (6) Yokohama 565,308.

Financial Integrity

All regulations and procedures for local finance in Japan are uniform and centralized in the Ministry of Finance and the Ministry of Internal Affairs in the central government. All municipal finance facilities follow the orders of the Ministry of Finance and the Ministry of Internal Affairs. For example, the creation of new taxes is not implemented without the approval of the central government. Therefore, all municipal finance revenues and expenditures are quite orderly. Regarding the construction part, a reconstruction bureau is attached to the Ministry of Internal Affairs after the earthquake. The reconstruction bureau and the city office are responsible for coordinating the size of the projects separately. However, the Japanese land tax still uses the land price of 30 to 40 years ago as the standard, which seems not very fair. When asked about it, the Japanese said that the Japanese government has been pursuing a tight fiscal policy in recent years, and it would cost a lot of money to conduct an investigation. Also, the Japanese government has been working hard to build since the earthquake. The current Tokyo has not only restored its former appearance, but has also become more beautiful, almost comparable to Washington and Paris. The most worthy of our reference in its restoration work is the issue of land zoning and reorganization. I will write another article to report to the people of the country.

Thoughts on this Trip: I am deeply impressed by the rapid development of the Japanese nation's undertakings on this trip. Our country has always criticized the Japanese for their short stature. In recent years, the Japanese government has been transforming the nation and promoting sports. Its speed of progress is enough to make people marvel. Older people may have short stature, but those under the age of 20 or 30 are tall and vigorous. Women also have large hands and feet, which are far beyond what Chinese women can hope to achieve. If our country does not promote sports and improve the race, then the outcome of international competition is a foregone conclusion.

The County's First District Requests a Delay in the Collection of Labor Service Taxes 27

The Minhang Town Hexiangqiao area in the county suffered a sudden hailstorm on the 7th of this month, causing damage to farmland, and the disaster was immediately apparent. However, after checking, there are still many labor service taxes for the 18th year that have not been completed, and the farmers are really unable to pay them. They should be granted a delay in collection to alleviate the people's difficulties. Director Wu believes that this matter concerns the national tax, and yesterday he reported the situation to the county government for verification and compliance.

Upper River Navigation News 29

The Taikoo Company's Wanliu steamer was rescued. The Wanliu steamer ran aground 45 li downstream of Chongqing, and the bottom of the ship was damaged. The passengers and cargo on board were rescued by the Nisshin Company's Yunyang Maru and Peiling Maru, which were passing by at the same time. Therefore, the passengers were safely rescued. On the 25th, the Taikoo Company's rescue steamer from Chongqing arrived at the scene. The Japanese steamer Yunyang and the steamer Fuling had already left the area and went to the port of Chongqing. The Wanliu steamer is still stranded, and the cargo on board is being unloaded.

Freight rates plummet. Since the resumption of navigation this year, the competition among Chinese and foreign merchant ships on the upper reaches of the Yangtze River has been fierce. There are 11 Chinese companies, but foreign ships from Britain, Japan, and the United States are more numerous. Chinese ships account for only two-tenths of the total. Yichong has always had the highest freight rates in the country. This year, Chinese ships resumed six routes first, and foreign merchants drastically reduced freight rates as a countermeasure against monopolies. It is reported that foreign merchants from Britain and Japan are operating in Yichang and Chongqing at a loss to make it difficult for Chinese ships to survive. The Shanghai-Chongqing direct routes of American merchants have also changed to charging 37.5% of the set price to compete.

Huangzhou Traffic. A decade ago, foreign merchants' Yangtze River steamers temporarily stopped at Huangzhou, Huangshigang, and other ports, and requested the British Navy to protect the ships. Now that Huangzhou, Huangshigang, and other places have returned to normal, foreign steamers have resumed normal stops at Huangzhou and other places. However, the naval escort in the Wuhan-Xunyang section is still in effect.

Request for protection. The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company of this port telegraphed the Anhui Provincial Government and the Capital Garrison Headquarters yesterday, requesting special protection for the upstream and downstream navigation of all Yangtze River steamers so that national port navigation can be revitalized, and passengers and goods can be conveniently loaded and unloaded. Only in this way can the lost navigation rights be recovered and the Jiangjing steamer incident be prevented from happening again. This telegram was sent out yesterday.

Hunan goods are rushed for shipment. The Hunan passengers and goods stranded in Shanghai are now being urged to load by telegram from Changsha. The six companies in this port are loading ships for upstream.

Circular Inoculation for Cholera Prevention by the Health Bureau 30

Yesterday, the Shanghai Municipal Police Bureau approved an official letter from the Health Bureau, which stated: "To facilitate citizens' awareness of cholera prevention injections, it is planned to use our bureau's mobile clinic vehicles from July 5th onwards to dispatch doctors and nurses to densely populated and lively areas in the southern and northern districts of Shanghai to inoculate the public with preventive injections. Accordingly, we request your bureau to inform all districts that when our bureau's vaccination vehicles arrive, the police on duty should provide assistance in taking care of and persuading citizens to get vaccinated for prevention. Please investigate and handle this matter, and enclose a copy of the location list and organization chart. Organization chart: (1) One doctor, nurse, and health patrol leader each. (2) Carry all kinds of injection equipment and propaganda materials (pictures and leaflets). (3) After the vehicle stops, the health patrol leader will distribute leaflets and, together with the local police on duty, persuade citizens to get vaccinated and encourage households to get vaccinated (it would be even better if the doctor gives a brief lecture). (4) Those who wish to be vaccinated should get on the vehicle in order and request vaccination without rushing. (5) The departure time can be changed according to the needs of each stationed location. (6) The number of people vaccinated at each stationed location should be listed separately and reported to the department daily. (7) Adults should be injected with 1 cc, and children should be injected with an appropriate amount according to their age and physique. (8) The reaction after the injection should be explained (such as swelling at the injection site, etc.). (9) Pay attention to stopping the vehicle for injection in crowded and lively places at any time. (10) Efforts should be made to increase the number of people vaccinated. Vaccination date and address schedule: Monday, 8:30 AM to 11:30 AM, Old Baidu Street, Xiaodongmen to Dongjiadu; 1:30 PM to 3:30 PM, Baoshan Road, Datong Road Bridge, Zhabei District; Tuesday, 8:30 AM to 11:30 AM, Old West Gate, Xiaocai Market, Tangjiawan Xiaocai Market, inside Xinbeimen; afternoon, Wuzhen Road Bridge, Zhabei District, Tanziwan Dayang Bridge; Wednesday, Gongyili Xiaocai Market, Xinzha Bridge North, Zhabei District; afternoon, Tie Men Bian, No. 16 Pu, West Gate Tram Station; Thursday, Hongzhen, Gongping Road, Wuhua Road, Xiangyan Bridge; afternoon, Chedaijiao, Qiujiang Road, Gonghe Road, Taiyang Temple; Friday, Guomalou Xiaocai Market, Xiaonanmen Xiaocai Market; afternoon, Hengfeng Road Bridge, Datong Road, Gonghe Road, Zhabei District; Saturday, Jiangyin Street, Daxing Street intersection, Hongqiao Xiaocai Market, Chenghuangmiao; afternoon, Gaochangmiao, Lao Zanhua, Xieqiao, Dapuqiao, etc. The above dates and times are all departing at 8:00 AM every morning, and each place is one hour; departing at 1:30 PM in the afternoon, and each place is also one hour."

Chamber of Commerce Protects Trademark for Domestically Produced Shirts and Socks 31

Yesterday, the Chamber of Commerce sent a letter to the Trademark Bureau to protect the "Lion Ball" trademark of the Jinglun Shirt and Sock Factory, stating: "On the 27th of this month, we received a letter from the Jinglun Shirt and Sock Factory stating that the Italian Yixing Company was dissatisfied with the Trademark Bureau's evaluation of the 'Lion Ball' trademark and requested a re-evaluation. We have copied a copy of the bureau's order and the company's request for re-evaluation and request your assistance, etc. After investigation, the main point of the Italian Yixing Company's request for re-evaluation is that they have abandoned the point of arguing about the 'actual first user' in Article Tian of the Trademark Law, and what they are trying their best to declare is the phrase 'continuously used in good faith for more than five years' in Article 4 of the Trademark Law. What they mean by 'good faith user' is nothing more than that 'the applicant was unaware that the respondent has been using the Lion Ball pattern for 30 years, otherwise the applicant would never have adopted this pattern.' And the proof that they would never adopt it is that 'the respondent has always threatened the applicant to stop using the pattern.' The important key to this case is whether the so-called proof that they 'continuously used it in good faith for more than five years before the implementation of the Trademark Law' is true. It should be known that before the implementation of the Trademark Law, the power to resolve this kind of dispute with foreigners did not lie with the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, but with the Mixed Court of the Concession. If Chinese merchants wanted to request the cessation of the pattern, firstly, the Trademark Law had not been promulgated at that time and there was no basis for it, and secondly, foreign-related lawsuits in the Mixed Court were all related to the interests of the consuls of various countries. As a result of the conflict of interests between China and the West, the verdicts of the judge and the presiding judge often differed, resulting in the police taking orders from the execution. Therefore, the 'danger' that the applicant mentioned can be definitely said not to have occurred. Anyone familiar with the situation of the Mixed Court at that time is familiar with and has heard of this. The applicant cannot make claims based on empty words. Therefore, according to the above conclusion, the only key point that the applicant relies on to prove that they 'continuously used it in good faith for more than five years before the implementation of the Trademark Law' has been fundamentally shaken, and their request to invoke Article 4 of the Trademark Law is naturally untenable. In addition to the factory submitting a written defense according to the law, in response to the letter, we hereby submit to your bureau in detail the opinions of our association on this case for your review and handling. This is extremely appreciated. Sincerely, to the Trademark Bureau."

Mitsui & Co. Sues for Goods 33

Lawyers for both sides debated qualifications yesterday.

The court set a deadline for correction.

Mitsui & Co. sued He Gengxing and Hong Cangting for failing to pay for goods. In the previous hearing by the Special District Court, Hong's lawyer, Mr. Zhang Rongxi, raised the issue of the legal status of the foreign merchant, arguing that the foreign merchant had not registered with the Chinese government and could not be recognized as a legal person. At that time, the presiding judge ruled that the plaintiff should correct the registration procedures and reschedule the hearing. This has been reported in this newspaper. The registration of foreign merchants is now trending towards becoming a reality from theory. The Ministry of Industry and Commerce of the National Government is also actively handling the registration of foreign merchants to meet the needs. Yesterday morning, Mr. Zhang Guoquan held another hearing on the case. After 9:00 AM, many Japanese people in Shanghai went to the Eighth Civil Court of the Special District Court to listen. Japanese newspapers and news agencies run by Japanese people all sent reporters to the court to record. Japanese news reporters have never paid as much attention to the court as Western newspapers. The fact that they sent reporters to the court for this case shows their attitude towards the case. At 10:30 AM, the case was heard. The defendant, He Gengxing, was still at large and did not arrive. The defendant, Hong Cangting, was still represented by Lawyer Zhang. First, Mr. Okamoto, the lawyer representing the plaintiff, the Japanese company Mitsui & Co., stood up and translated, saying that Lawyer Zhang had raised the issue of legal person in the previous hearing as a countermeasure. After the presiding judge ruled, our lawyer collected all the materials and described the reasons in detail. In addition to what is stated in writing, I will add an oral statement. According to the defendant's lawyer, any foreign firm that has not registered has no right to sue, and a foreign legal person who wants to sue in a Chinese court should register in accordance with Chinese law. Our lawyer believes that any foreign legal person who still enjoys consular jurisdiction is not bound by Chinese law. Therefore, since the signing of the so-called unequal treaties, this problem has never occurred. If you want to change the course of action, you should first start with the so-called unequal treaties. The first article of the Anglo-Japanese Treaty of Commerce and the US-Japanese Treaty of Commerce both stipulate that the people of the two contracting countries should abide by all the laws of the other contracting country when doing business in the other contracting country, and should enjoy the same rights and obligations as the people of any contracting country. However, the Sino-Japanese Treaty of Commerce does not have this provision. Therefore, Japanese merchants are not bound by Chinese law, and the National Government has never objected to the rights enjoyed by Japan. Other Chinese courts have also never ordered Japanese people to be subject to Chinese law. This is because the Sino-Japanese Treaty still exists. Moreover, the Chinese Civil Law and other laws do not apply to the people of countries that enjoy jurisdiction, so Chinese courts have never denied the legal status of foreign merchants because they have not registered in China. The lawyer then cited several types of laws, such as the precedent of the Supreme Court, saying that since the Chinese court had previously recognized foreign merchants as plaintiffs, it naturally recognized that they had the right to sue and had legal person status. Moreover, Mitsui & Co. had registered in its own country and obtained legal person status, so it should be recognized as a legal person in any country. After searching through Chinese law, there is no clear provision on how foreign legal persons should register. As for the existence of capacity, according to Chinese law, the court should investigate ex officio and should not wait for the other party to raise it. In the past, there were many foreign merchants who sued in Chinese courts, and this kind of problem never occurred. Since the Chinese court accepted foreign merchants' lawsuits, it had already recognized that they had the right to sue. Recently, the Supreme Court accepted a case where the plaintiff was also a Japanese merchant, and the Supreme Court never inquired about the qualifications, and the Japanese merchant was an unregistered merchant in China. Even your court has recently accepted foreign merchants' lawsuits without any such objections. Although the articles formulated by the Public Concession, which contain the language of applying Chinese law, have been withdrawn, it means that they include old precedents or customs that have not been recognized by the government. As for those bound by treaties, Chinese law does not apply. Even if Chinese law applies to foreign merchants, foreign merchants do not need to register in China. According to the provisions of the Registration Law, registration should be requested from the local government office, but our lawyer has inquired about the registration procedures from your court, and your court has not yet prepared. From this, it can be seen that China does not really want foreign merchants to register, and it can be seen that Chinese law is still in its infancy. In short, in this case, (1) Chinese law cannot be applied to countries that enjoy treaty rights; (2) incomplete Chinese laws cannot be applied to foreigners. The presiding judge listened attentively to this point and felt that Lawyer Okamoto's words were extremely flawed. If he continued to tolerate him, he might become even more presumptuous, so he quickly corrected him and said: "What this court wants to discuss is the law, but what your lawyer said mostly involves jurisdiction. You don't know that jurisdiction is a diplomatic issue and is actually wrong. Your lawyer is concerned about the fact that Japan is a country that enjoys consular jurisdiction. From a legal point of view, I believe that jurisdiction is not a natural right, but is constituted by a treaty. The Sino-Japanese Treaty expired last year. This court has received instructions from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to guide the handling of litigation by the people of countries whose treaties have expired in accordance with the seven articles of the measures stipulated by the Ministry of Foreign Affairs. The people of all countries whose treaties have expired are treated the same as the people of countries that have no treaties. This kind of measure is not only for Japan. However, since Japan is a country whose treaty has expired, it should be handled in accordance with these measures. Later, when observing the point that the consuls of those whose treaties have expired all came to the hearing based on the old treaty because the new treaty had not been concluded, until the National Government clearly ordered the abolition of consular jurisdiction in China on the first day of this year and re-established the measures for post-restitution. This court has always advocated that anyone under the jurisdiction of this court, regardless of their nationality, should be treated the same as Chinese people. Chinese law applies to this court. The Japanese consul also signed the agreement to reorganize the provisional court. Now, suppose a Chinese company sues this court in the name of a legal person. It should of course register with the Ministry of Industry and Commerce. At this time when the old treaty has expired and the new treaty has not been signed, we should urgently abide by Chinese law. The Company Law has been promulgated, although it has not yet been implemented. However, there are still company regulations that can be used. How can it be said that there is no law? The second point that your lawyer argues is that Chinese law is incomplete. But as far as the law of this case is concerned, I think it is sufficient to make considerable references. It must be known that company registration is different from foundation registration. Company registration should be submitted to the Ministry of Industry and Commerce and does not fall within the scope of the local government office. As for the ability to sue, it is true that the court should investigate ex officio. However, in the past, since the other party did not raise any objections, why should the government be so picky? In the future, I will pay more attention to this matter. If any discoveries are made, I will give temporary relief. However, the right to sue cannot be deprived because they do not have legal person status. However, the plaintiff's written reasons are lengthy and have not been carefully reviewed. I am now pointing out the mistakes that have been found. As for whether there are any inappropriate points, I will not discuss them for the time being." Next, Lawyer Zhang refuted each of the points made by Okamoto, stating briefly that although the reasons stated by the plaintiff's lawyer were extremely lengthy, they were also extremely inadequate. All the answers were nothing more than (1) which is stronger, the effect of law or treaty? According to international law, treaties that concern the interests of the people should only take effect after being passed by the country. Laws can abolish treaties, and treaties can also abolish laws. New laws can also abolish old treaties. Even Japanese jurists recognize this theory. (2) In international law, the four characters "consular jurisdiction" cannot be recognized. Moreover, jurisdiction has now been explicitly abolished, and the Sino-Japanese Treaty has also expired and the new treaty has not been concluded. How can Mitsui & Co. continue to invoke jurisdiction? However, let's talk about the effect of jurisdiction. It can only affect foreigners who are defendants. If a foreigner is a plaintiff, they must sue the Chinese court in accordance with Chinese law. Even if they have jurisdiction, they cannot be exempted. Since Mitsui is the plaintiff, it should be handled in accordance with Chinese law. The plaintiff's lawyer said that foreign legal persons have previously sued in China, so the Chinese court has recognized them as legal persons. They don't know that most foreigners are in the Public Concession. Although the Public Concession was established based on the Yangjingbang Regulations, it has lost its legal status since the Xinhai Revolution because it was managed by foreigners. Therefore, the Supreme Court ruled in the sixth year that the judgments of the Public Concession are not effective. Although it was later changed to a provisional court, it was only a change between the local government and the consular corps. It was actually a temporary situation and still had no legitimate status in law. Now, a special representative of the state has been appointed to establish an agreement organization and a formal court. All Chinese laws, whether substantive law or procedural law, apply to it. All the bad habits of the past cannot be used. If those foreigners sue your court, they should abide by Chinese law, otherwise it would be illegal. Chinese law stipulates that those who do not have the ability to sue should have their lawsuits rejected. (3) The plaintiff's lawyer also said that Chinese law is incomplete and that they have no way to obtain legal person status. This shows that they have no understanding of Chinese law as a whole. As far as our lawyer knows, Chinese law is extremely complete, extremely broad, and has many advantages. It is better than the laws of any country. There are many legal provisions for foreign merchants to obtain legal person status in accordance with Chinese law. The lawyer then pointed out the applicable legal provisions one by one, saying that anyone, regardless of their nationality, can obtain the same status and rights as Chinese legal persons if they follow the law. What they call incomplete is really a frog in a well. The lawyer then explained in detail Article 8 of the Company Regulations, which states that "before registration, they shall not resist third parties." Finally, they requested the court to decide on a period of time so that the plaintiff could correct the procedures as the case cannot be delayed again and again. If the correction is not made by the deadline, their lawsuit will be rejected. The presiding judge then ordered that the hearing be rescheduled to July 30 and that the plaintiff should correct the procedures within the deadline before announcing the adjournment. It was already one o'clock in the afternoon.

A Record of the Departure of the Asia Walking Group Yesterday 34

The Friendship Travel Group gave very earnest farewell remarks.

Nine young men and women of the Chinese Youth Asia Walking Group gathered at the North Station at 9:00 AM yesterday morning. They were carrying luggage and blankets, water bottles, oil cloths, backpacks, compasses, and other items, each weighing 30 pounds. They were all dressed in yellow serge scout uniforms and wore white copper basin hats. Teachers and students from various schools and representatives from various organizations went to see them off, which was very enthusiastic. First, photographers from various newspapers took photos of each individual, and then took a group photo with the guests. They also asked the stationmaster and the general manager of the transportation department to sign and verify the departure. At the time of departure, the Friendship Travel Group elected Huang Xincun to give a farewell speech, imitating the meaning of farewell remarks of the ancients. He said briefly that the news of your grand tour has spread all over the country and has touched the dreams of Chinese youth. It is a great honor for the Chinese nation, and there are three female comrades who are fighting for freedom. It can be said to be a sweet long journey. We originally intended to buy many gifts to pay tribute, but we thought that the group rules limited the weight, so we could not fulfill our wish. We specially entrusted me to express a few words as follows: (1) Study the subjects of road education and social universities. (2) How to travel economically, save time and energy. (3) Awaken the public everywhere and pay attention to the people's illnesses. (4) Experiment with travel hygiene, do not drink dirty water or eat raw and cold food in hot weather. (5) Talk less, do more, run less, rest more. (6) Help each other, cooperate, and accept the advice of elders. (7) Cherish the reputation of the group and respect public decisions. (8) Visit and collect botanical specimens everywhere and send good news to the Shanghai Report, etc. When departing, the Oriental Bookstore Publishing House set off a large number of firecrackers, and the sound of explosions was endless. Hundreds of people sent them off. The group lined up and marched west with a tragic and silent attitude. When passing by Guanghua University, they specially prepared tea and snacks to welcome them. When passing by Longhua, they encountered a heavy rain, but they still marched forward in the rain. Last night, they stayed overnight in the fields near Xinzhuang. They set out at 5:00 AM this morning and walked to Songjiang, where they were received by Songjiang Girls' High School or will stay for a few days.

Case of the Protection Corps Shooting Li Zhonghua 35

Seeking Handwriting from Loan Shark Account Books

Prosecutor Changes Course After Argument

The case of Li Zhonghua (also known as Li Zhongyi), a loan shark, who was shot in the right arm by the Shanghai South City Protection Corps while attempting to apprehend bandits, was brought to court by Li's wife, Li Wangshi. After questioning and gathering evidence, the District Court Prosecutor's Office charged the Protection Corps with suspicion of murder and filed a public lawsuit. The Criminal Court judges then conducted a public trial, ordering both parties to present their witnesses to testify to everything. The details of which have been reported in previous newspapers. Now, we will provide a detailed account of the causes, consequences, and yesterday's continued trial, including Li Zhonghua's detention.

Chen Liangsheng Receives Threatening Letter. Chen Liangsheng (previously mistakenly reported as Chen Liangyu), a local resident, is 40 years old and lives at No. 49 Zhao Jiawan Street, Xiaonanmen. As a silk merchant, he is quite well-off, making him a target for bandits. In March and April of this year, he received three threatening letters from bandits. Two of the letters were written in ink, and one in blue ink, demanding 600 yuan. They also threatened that if he didn't pay, they would proceed with a kidnapping, with a minimum ransom of 10,000 yuan. The payment location was repeatedly reported as the front of the Zhengde School on Xiaozha Bridge Street, Xiaonanmen, with a red wood shop identified by a newspaper. After receiving the letter, Chen immediately reported to the seventh squad of the Protection Corps and requested an investigation.

Li Zhonghua Places a Newspaper. After receiving the report, Ma Wenda, the captain of the seventh squad, secretly dispatched platoon leader Jin Shunyi to supervise corps members Gu Guo'an, Lin Jinxian, and others, all in disguise, to the location designated by the bandits at 10:00 PM on April 21 (the date agreed upon by the bandits) for an ambush. At the appointed time, Li Zhonghua arrived and took a newspaper from his bag, placing it on the red wood. Unexpectedly, the wind blew it to the ground. Li picked up the newspaper and placed it back on the red wood, then picked up a brick to weigh it down to prevent it from being blown away by the wind. The corps members witnessed this and rushed out, shouting for him to stop. Li made a gesture to shoot, and the corps members, in self-defense, had to shoot, injuring his right arm. At the time, Li was detained by the first district, third precinct, and then sent to Shanghai Hospital for treatment of his gunshot wound.

Engaged in Loan Sharking for Years. Li Zhonghua (also known as Li Zhongyi, Zhongyi, and Li Zhongyi) is from Zhili Province, 37 years old. He was formerly a police officer in the Security Squad of the former Police Department. After leaving the police force, he made a living as a loan shark, living with his wife, Wang, at No. 37 North Tangfang Lane, Xiaonanmen. He has over 100 borrowers, making a considerable profit. It is believed that Li has been lending money for over ten years. Therefore, most of the old goods vendors and brokers in the South City area know Li Zhonghua. However, his reputation is quite bad, and it was unexpected that he would engage in such extortion.

Public Security Bureau Alleges Li Was Wronged. After Li was injured and sent to the hospital, his wife, Li Wangshi, was encouraged by others to file a complaint with the District Court Prosecutor's Office, claiming that the Protection Corps should not have opened fire rashly and injured an innocent citizen, requesting an investigation. Prosecutor Xu Heling ordered the summoning of Protection Corps platoon leader Jin Shunchang, Gu Guo'an, and others for questioning. For the sake of caution, a letter was sent to the Public Security Bureau for verification. The bureau replied, stating that Li Zhonghua's behavior was usually very good and that he had no illegal activities. Based on the reply, the prosecutor filed a public lawsuit, accusing Jin Shunchang and Gu Guo'an of committing the crime of murder under Article 282, Section 2 of the Criminal Law.

Handwriting on Small Account Books. After the incident, Ma Wenda, captain of the seventh squad of the Protection Corps, paid close attention to investigating the facts, collecting all kinds of evidence. He led corps members Yu Ruixiang, Peng Rongquan, and others to the homes of Li Zhonghua's borrowers, such as Kang Jiabao, Zhou Abing, Gao Fuxing, and others, to investigate and confirm that Li Zhonghua had loaned them money.

Page 16

The printing of money was indeed true. Captain Ma sent a letter to the first district party headquarters, explaining the situation to Kang Jiabao and others, and brought back four small account books used by Li Zhonghua for printing money to the party headquarters, giving them a receipt. The party headquarters then sent a letter along with the four small account books to Captain Ma. It was discovered that one of the account books was written in blue ink, and the depth of the color matched the blue ink threatening letter sent to Chen Liangsheng's house. The most surprising thing was that the character "jia" (家, home) in Kang Jiabao's name matched the character "jia" (家, home) in "Zhao Jiawan Street" on Chen's letter, proving that the threatening letter was indeed written by Li Zhonghua. Captain Ma immediately submitted the account books and the letter from the party headquarters to lawyer Tang Yingsong, who presented them in court during the first public trial and requested an examination.

Presenting Evidence of Interest Rates. The first public trial was on the morning of the 14th of this month. The judge paid close attention to the handwriting on the account books. At that time, Li Zhonghua was ordered to write down the addresses of the witnesses. Li claimed that he could not write and that his arm was injured and he could not hold a pen. After the court adjourned, Li immediately went around collecting his account books from all the debtors. The debtors were surprised as to why he would take back the account books when the money had not been paid off. It was said that it was difficult to collect all the account books because there were many household names, and it took until dawn the next day to collect them all. This is worth studying. During the second Criminal Court hearing, the witnesses presented by Li Zhonghua all claimed that they had borrowed money from Li, but it was not loan sharking, but rather interest was charged at two percent per month. In fact, their testimony was contradictory. For example, if they borrowed ten yuan, the monthly interest rate should be twenty cents, but the witnesses claimed that it was twenty cents.

Detailed Interrogation of Li Zhonghua. Yesterday morning at 10:00 AM, Judge Wu Zhen and Prosecutor Xu Heling opened the second courtroom. The officer first ordered Li Zhonghua to the dock and asked: (Q) Do you know Kang Jiabao? (A) I know him. (Q) Has he borrowed money from you? (A) No. (Q) Did he borrow 15,000 cash from you in February and 10,000 cash in March? (A) No. (Q) If you didn't lend him money, why did he say you lent him money? Moreover, there is your account book. (A) The account book is not mine. The officer said, "Kang Jiabao testified in court that you are a big man. What do you have to say?" (A) I have been in the South City for over ten years, so they know me. (Q) Did you lend money to Zhou Abing? (A) Yes, he borrowed five yuan from me and has already paid it back. Later, I introduced someone named Ma to lend him money. The officer showed Zhou Abing's account book to Li. (A) It's not mine. (Q) Have you lent money to Gao Fuxing? (A) I don't know him. The officer said, "He said you lent him money. How can you say you don't know him?" He also showed Gao Fuxing's account book to him. (A) It's not mine. I lent money at two percent interest, not loan sharking. They are framing me." The officer ordered Jin Shunchang and Gu Guo'an to the dock and asked, "What else do you have to say?" Jin and Gu replied, "Nothing." At this point, lawyer Tang stood up and said, "The characters 'jia' and 'bao' (家保, home protection) on Kang Jiabao's account book are exactly the same as the characters 'jia' and 'bao' on the threatening letter, and they are both written in blue ink. The court should pay attention to this." The officer asked Prosecutor Xu to stand up and argue, stating, "Based on the Public Security Bureau's reply, Li Zhonghua is a good man, so the prosecutor believes that the Protection Corps is suspected of murder and filed a public lawsuit. However, the results of the trial, based on the party headquarters' letter and the money printing account books, show that Li Zhonghua is strongly suspected of handwriting. However, Jin Shunchang and Gu Guo'an did not have any major circumstances. Only that they did not report the arrest to the police station beforehand. The presiding judge should decide." At this point, lawyer Tang stood up and argued, stating, "The premise should be whether the threatening letter was written by Li Zhonghua. The actions of the defendants Jin Shunchang, Gu Guo'an, etc. are completely legal. As for not reporting to the police, it is within the scope of administration. Moreover, the handwriting matches completely. At the time, Li Zhonghua's every move, time, location, and objects were exactly the same as the threatening letter. Furthermore, the witnesses presented by Li Zhonghua testified that the time was 7:00 or 8:00 PM, but the incident occurred before 11:00 PM. The court should declare them innocent." Then, Feng Buqing, the lawyer hired by Li Zhonghua, stood up and requested a private lawsuit, stating that Li Zhonghua could not live after being shot in the arm and should be paid 15 yuan per month for living expenses for twenty years. The officer then announced that the debate in this case was concluded and that the verdict would be announced at 2:00 PM on the 30th of this month. Jin Shunchang and Gu Guo'an were ordered to leave. Li Zhonghua was ordered to be taken down and detained by the bailiffs. After the court adjourned, Prosecutor Xu opened a special investigation court and ordered Li Zhonghua to be brought in for questioning. He ruled that he should be returned to custody to await a thorough investigation.

Qian Jiagen, the Culprit in the Assassination of Shen Dingyi, Escorted Through Shanghai 36

Death to the Murderer is Expected

Qian Jiagen, the main culprit in the assassination of Shen Dingyi, a member of the First Central Committee, is 26 years old this year and a native of Sheng County. In 1928, he assassinated Shen in front of the Reformatory and fled to the Harbin Shipyard to work as a laborer, intending to change his name and escape justice. Unexpectedly, he was exposed by a close friend. The Zhejiang Provincial Government sent a letter to the Harbin authorities requesting the arrest of Qian Jiagen. He has now been escorted south and passed through Shanghai yesterday. Qian was escorted to the District Court for temporary detention so that the Zhejiang authorities could transfer him back for trial. However, Qian Jiagen's attitude was very calm, stating that "Death to the murderer is expected."

Nantong Bandit Pan Zihong 37

Arrested for Evil Deeds in Pudong

Pan Zihong, a notorious bandit from Jinsha Town, Nantong County, was wanted for multiple cases of kidnapping and murder. He fled to Shanghai and hid in the home of his fellow villager, Gu Longsheng, in Lujiazai, Pudong, disguised as a worker and gambling all day long. On the night of the 22nd of this month, he gathered to gamble at Gu's place again. Chen Guangyan, a detective from the Third District Public Security Bureau, learned of this and secretly reported it to the District Chief, who dispatched police officers to arrest Pan. According to Pan's confession, he is 29 years old and from Tongzhou. He came to Shanghai last month to find work but was unsuccessful and lived idly at his friend's place, denying being a bandit. The District Chief ordered him to be temporarily detained and sent a letter to the Ninth District Office in Tongzhou to investigate whether he was a law-abiding citizen. Yesterday, a reply was received from the head of the office, stating that Pan Zihong was indeed a wanted criminal in Tongzhou for multiple cases and had been repeatedly sought without success. Please escort him for questioning and trial. District Chief Zhang immediately prepared a document ordering the transfer of the bandit Pan to the Public Security Bureau for questioning and trial.

Jail Guards Strike 38

One Arrested Out of More Than Fifty

The Da Wan Bao reported that fifty jail guards and police officers at the Huade Road prison went on strike yesterday because the leader they had elected was not appointed by the police authorities, and the newly appointed leader was not of the same rank as them. In the afternoon, they gathered at the British Consulate General to meet with officials and demand the replacement of the new leader. When Consul Bailun came out to inquire about the matter and advised them to abide by discipline and return to duty, the guards refused. Chief Inspector Qiu Laide ordered them to report for duty before 6:00 PM, otherwise they would be fired. The crowd still lingered at the consulate and dispersed after 6:00 PM. This morning, they went to the consulate again and were joined by some sympathizers and agitators, adding several demands. Gan Naitai, the deputy chief inspector in charge of the special police officers, ordered everyone to gather in a circle and listen to Consul Bailun's advice. During Consul Bailun's speech, the head of the prison, Lusi, arrested Bu Xin, a sympathizer among the dismissed jail guards and police officers, accusing him of inciting arson at the consulate. It is said that he will be sent to the British Public Hall for trial on Monday. After Consul Bailun finished his speech, everyone dispersed. Because they failed to report for duty last night, their names have been automatically removed from the police station's roster.

National Photography Exhibition, Day Two 41

Closing at 6:00 PM Today

The [Third National Photography Exhibition], initiated by the China Photographic Society, opened the day before yesterday. Yesterday was the second day, and it was also Saturday, so the number of visitors was exceptionally crowded. Many young ladies and celebrities attended. Throughout the day, there were more than 5,000 visitors. Those from the photography world who attended were Shen Gao, Guo Shuliang, Peng Wangshi, Hu Boxiang, and others. Those from the art world were Yang Qingpan, Zhang Guangyu, Zhenyu Kunzhong, Lu Shaofei, and others. From the business world, Zhao Jinqing, and others. From the press world, Ge Gongzhen and others. All were entertained by Lin Zecang from the Association and all praised the progress of the works in this exhibition compared to the past, especially the beautification of light. There were also many photography enthusiasts who circled the venue three or five times without stopping. Yesterday, as many as six publishing houses went to the exhibition to take photos and request photos. The Shen Bao, selected 17 photos by Mr. Ge and took photos of the exhibition venue. The News Daily's Photography Era sold 17 frames. The Red Tile magazine, twelve frames. The Wenhua magazine, ten frames. The Arts Friend, twenty-five frames. As for the best works from past photography exhibitions and competitions and the best works from this exhibition, they will be compiled into the [Chinese Photography Yearbook] and published by the publishing department of the China Photographic Society at No. 56 Nanjing Road. It is heard that the photography exhibition is scheduled to close at 6:00 PM today and will not be extended. It is expected that today, as it is Sunday, will be another grand occasion. The exhibition closed at 8:00 PM last night.

Jiangbei People Clash with Guangdong People 42

Minor Cause, Many Injuries

At around 6:00 PM last night, there was an armed clash between Jiangbei people and Guangdong people on the vacant lot at the end of Dong Zhangjia Road, Zhonghongqiao. There were about one hundred and seventy or eighty people on both sides, using iron rulers and sharp blades as weapons. Fortunately, passersby reported the incident to the Linping Road police station of the Third Precinct of the Fifth District Public Security Bureau, and all the police officers set out and arrested nineteen people involved. Ten of them were seriously injured and were sent to Tongren Hospital for treatment. The cause of this incident was minor, but the two sides were eager to fight privately, which led to a major disaster. It turned out that Liu Yongfu, a Jiangbei person, opened a pancake shop on Zhangqiao Road. Yesterday evening, after finishing work, he was walking on the road when he saw a rental sign posted on the door of Tongliyuan Heji Niupihao (leather shop) and craned his neck to look. At that time, Dai Yin, the Cantonese doorman of Tongliyuan, was particularly attentive to the doorway because he had been robbed a few days ago. Seeing Liu pacing and staring at the door, he questioned him. The two sides could not understand each other and suddenly started arguing, followed by physical violence. The workers of the leather factory heard the noise and gathered to watch, joining in the fight. Even more people from Jiangbei came to rescue Liu Yongfu, quickly gathering more than a hundred people. The Cantonese side also had sixty or seventy people. Fortunately, a passerby, Chen Wan, went to the Linqing Road police station of the Third Precinct of the Fifth District Public Security Bureau to report the incident. The police officers immediately went to disperse the crowd and arrested the perpetrators. However, when the police arrived, the two sides had already had some contact, and weapons such as sharp knives and long spears had already been used. By the time the police arrived at the end of Zhangqiao Road, the clever ones had already escaped without a trace. Only those who were injured and stubborn were arrested and taken to the station. The main person involved, Liu Yongfu, was injured all over his body and, along with Sun Zitian, was sent to Tongren Hospital for treatment with Ye Yaoji, Yang Zanbian, Wang Xin, Cai Busheng, Dai Jin, Yang Fa, and others. Among them, Liu Yongfu, Cai Busheng, and Sun Zitian were from Jiangbei, while the rest were Cantonese. Others who were slightly injured or not injured at all included Dai Yin, the instigator, and accomplices Zhong Hua, Li Jun, Liu Jian, Li Long, Cai Bang, Yang Fa, Zhang Yaoheng, Li Ruyou, Huo Zhishui, Yang Dan, and others, a total of eleven people. There was also a Zhu Changshun, who surrendered himself to the station. Among the above-mentioned ten people, Zhang Yaoheng, Li Ruyou, Huo Zhishui, and Yang Dan were all members of the Tongqunle Martial Arts Association on Qiujiang Road. They claimed that the long spears and knives they brought were because they heard that their fellow villagers were surrounded by the Jiangbei gang and hired cars to transport long spears and short knives to rescue them. As for the cause of the incident, the Cantonese side claimed that the Jiangbei people had been extorting money, and Liu Yongfu was suspected of theft. Both sides insisted on their own versions, which were quite different. However, it is undeniable that the two sides had been harboring resentment for a long time.

Lu Gengrong Case Reopened for Debate Yesterday 43

Debate Concluded, Verdict Tomorrow

The case of the love affair between the master and servant, Huang and Lu, regarding the part of Lu Gengrong helping to steal, was returned to the High Court for retrial by the Supreme Court. Yesterday afternoon at 2:00 PM, Zhao Zhengzhang, acting presiding judge of the First Criminal Court of the High Court, together with prosecutor Jin Henian, assessor judges, and court clerks, reopened the debate court. Huang Zhushi, mother of Huang Huiru, was summoned. Lu Zhenrong and Lu's defense lawyer, Song Mingxun, also appeared in court. About 300 people were in attendance. The hearing lasted about an hour before it ended. Because the case attracted special attention from society, the judge interrogated in detail. The details are as follows. After the court opened, Lu Gengrong was first brought to the court. Judge Zhao asked his name, age, and place of origin, and then announced the reason for reopening the debate. Then, Huang Zhushi was summoned for questioning. Huang Zhushi testified that she was 49 years old, from Wuxing, Zhejiang. She originally lived on Hed Road in Shanghai and now lives at No. 23 West Zhijia Lane in Suzhou. The official asked if Huang Huiru was dead or not. She replied that she had died long ago. The official asked if the "Third Miss" reported in the newspaper was her niece. She replied that it was a relative who lived with her. There was no one left in her family, so she lived with her. The official asked when Lu Gengrong came to her house and what she meant by hiring lawyer Pan Chenge today. She replied that she hired a lawyer to prove that Lu Gengrong had indeed taken the things out and that he was not wronged. Lu Gengrong came to her house on September 13, 1927, to work as a tea server. The official asked when Huang Huiru and Lu Gengrong started their relationship and whether it was in January 1928. She replied that she did not know at first, but later she knew after Lu Gengrong and her daughter Huiru left together. On the twelfth day, Gengrong went out and did not show her the things as usual. She suspected something and questioned her daughter, asking when Gengrong left. She replied that it was 4:00 PM on the twelfth. Later, when the lights came on at 6:00 or 7:00 PM, she discovered that something was missing. She asked Huiru, and Huiru said that Lu Gengrong had ordered her to take it, and now Lu Gengrong had taken it away. This was said in the room, and no one else heard it. At that time, Jin Ma and A Jin were both working downstairs and probably did not hear it. The official asked when Huiru told her about the things being deposited in Qu Xingtai's carpentry shop. She replied that Huiru was unwilling to speak at first, but she bought them after she scolded her. She spoke one or two days later. The official asked if Huiru left on the thirteenth, how could she speak to her one or two days later? Perhaps it was at night on the twelfth? She replied no, she spoke after the District Court verdict. The official asked if there was no such statement in the first trial court record. She asked if she had stated this in the first trial complaint. She replied that she had. Today, she said that Huiru only spoke to her after the first trial verdict. When did Huiru tell her? She replied that she did not remember. The official asked if Huiru had not seen her when she went out. She replied that she saw Huiru go downstairs early in the morning on the thirteenth. At that time, the servants had not gotten up, but she had not slept all night. She chased her downstairs, but she had already gone out. She chased her to the door, but she was no longer to be seen. According to people nearby, there was a car, but she did not see it herself. This was because Huiru was fast. In her opinion, it was not easy to hide things in summer clothes. The official asked if she had shouted at her when she chased her that day. She replied that she had shouted at her, but she had already gone out and did not answer. The official asked where the jewelry box was placed. She replied that it was in the room under the bed, against the north. The official asked how many people there were in total. She replied that there were only her mother and daughter. The official asked if Lu Gengrong had gone upstairs on the twelfth. She replied that he had not gone upstairs. The official asked if there was a small leather box that she said she gave to him. She replied that there was. The official asked why she did not report the theft at 7:00 PM that day when she knew that things were missing. She replied that it was because it was late. The official asked why she said it was late at 7:00 PM. She asked where Qu Xingtai's carpentry shop was. She replied that she did not know. She only found out later because she did not go out much. Later, she went to inquire and he had moved and was no longer on Hed Road. The official asked if she could find Qu Xingtai now. She replied that she could not find him. She did not even know if Lu Gengrong had any cousins ​​there. The official asked if she said in the first trial complaint that Lu Gengrong deposited the things in Qu Xingtai's carpentry shop with his cousin Lu Yongqing. Now she said she did not know about it. How could she say that? Was Jin Ma and A Jin summoned today? She replied that they had not been summoned. Jin Ma quit last year and A Jin went to the countryside in 1928. The official asked if they could not be found. The official asked if Huiru had always protected Lu Gengrong in previous court trials. Why did she not help her mother instead? She replied yes, but Huiru had cried out in grievance when she was seriously ill, saying that she had been deceived by Lu Gengrong. The official asked when she had repented. She replied that it was in the hospital. He said that he had a good life at home, but he did not expect to be in danger after being deceived. She asked me to take him home, and he died on the road at 4:00 PM that afternoon. Lu Gengrong took the things because my daughter Huiru did not want to take my things. After Lu Gengrong took them away, Lu Gengrong's cousin Lu Yongqing kept them for him. The official asked if there was any evidence that Lu Gengrong took the things to prosecute him. She replied that it was not a miscarriage of justice. She did not have anything else to say. At that point, the official asked again what she meant by hiring a lawyer today. Did she want him to testify? She replied that she did not call him to testify. The official asked if all the words she said were her own and did not need him to say on her behalf. She replied yes. The official asked if she had anything else to say. She replied that her family was now ruined and she did not have the face to see anyone in Shanghai, so she avoided going to Suzhou. She asked the court to judge Gengrong's crime. She did not have anything else to say. Next, Lu Gengrong was summoned for questioning. The official asked if he had heard what Huang Zhushi had said just now and what he had to say. Lu replied that it was a miscarriage of justice. First, on the fourth day after I came out of the exchange, I went to Huang's house to return the bedding. The small box I took out was given to me by Madam. Madam checked the contents of the box, which were clothes and other items. Also, Madam saw me leave at 9:00 AM when I left. Now she said it was 4:00 PM, which is not the right time. Second, Qu Xingtai's carpentry shop had been doing business with Huang's family long before I went to Huang's house. Now Huang Zhushi said she did not know them. This is the second point that is not right. As for my relationship with Miss, it has been stated in previous court trials. Moreover, she now said that Jin Ma and A Jin were nowhere to be found, which shows that Huang Zhushi was not telling the truth. Then, Prosecutor Jin stood up to argue, stating that the case was reopened for a more detailed investigation. Based on today's results, there was no change from the previous argument. Finally, the presiding judge ordered the court clerk to read the testimony of Huang Zhushi and Lu Gengrong, who signed their names separately. Lu Gengrong also stated that he had been in prison for two years and asked the court to appeal for grievances. The presiding judge then announced that the debate in this case was concluded and that the verdict would be announced at 2:00 PM on the 30th of this month. The court adjourned and Lu Gengrong was returned to custody.

Shanghai Volunteer Corps Chinese Company Ge Lei Lie Cup Competition Report 44

Wu Guanghua Stands Out

The Ge Lei Lie Cup competition is a shooting competition that the Shanghai Volunteer Corps Chinese Company places great emphasis on, so they have always been at the top of various competitions. Taking the Ge Lei Lie Cup as an example, Shanghai has won for many years. The Singapore branch has already won four times. Last year, the team won with a score of 777 points against Singapore's 759 points. This year, the Shanghai competition was held at the shooting range on the morning of the 27th. The sun was scorching and the heat was oppressive. The competitors did not let the sweat pouring down their faces diminish their courage. They were all determined, solemn, and brave. It was heard that the team had specially invited General Headquarters Hu Guojun, Akio staff officer Henry Kreiff, and officials and clerks, as well as the competition gun club's committee member Kalaso and the team's captain Wang Yanqing to the scene to judge and score. It was learned that the team's shooting performance in this year's competition was even better than last year. The best shooter was Wu Guanghua, a private in the team, who scored 91 points. It is said that this competitor has been in the team for less than three years and has already achieved this first-class result, which is truly commendable. Sergeant Wang Zixiang scored 82 points. Lieutenant Chen Shixia and trainee He Bingcheng each scored 80 points. Military officer Li Yushu and trainee Mao Hanqing each scored 78 points. Sergeant Zhang Jianqing scored 77 points. Private Yao Liangfu and trainee Xi Yiwu each scored 76 points. Trainee Zhang Qixiang scored 74 points. The total score of the sixty members was 792 points.

All Zhejiang Relief Association Performing Opera to Raise Funds 45

Two Days and Two Nights: July 4th and 5th

Distinguished amateur actors will perform Peking Opera

Each ticket comes with a complimentary "Kindness Fruit" coupon

The All Zhejiang Relief Association in Shanghai has previously issued "Kindness Fruit" coupons, priced at five yuan each, with books and paintings offered as gifts to encourage sales. All proceeds went towards disaster relief. Due to widespread disasters in various provinces and the ongoing war, the association has been tirelessly promoting the coupons, but many remain unsold. Now that the drawing date is approaching, the Standing Committee of the association has devised a plan to raise funds through opera performances. They have entrusted individuals to seek assistance and have successfully secured commitments from various amateur actors to perform Peking Opera at the Grand Theater on San Ma Road on the nights of July 4th and 5th. Each opera ticket will be sold for five yuan and will include a complimentary "Kindness Fruit" coupon. The association has extended invitations to prominent figures in politics, renowned personalities, wealthy merchants, and elegant ladies. Names like Tianju Jushi Zhang Xiaolin, Yuan Ludeng, Zhang Weiru, Qiu Jianfei, Hong Yanbin, Xie Baosheng, Rong Boming, He Wuliang, and Sun Lanting, as well as Mrs. Wang Xiaolai, Mrs. Du Yuesheng, Ms. Jiang Wencai, and Ms. Xiao Lan, are all highly respected. These individuals, who normally would not readily perform on stage, are making an exception at the request of the Relief Association, gracing the stage with their presence. It is believed that those who purchase tickets, spending a mere five yuan, will not only contribute to the disaster relief effort but also appreciate high art and have the chance to win a prize. It is anticipated that the bustling streets of Shanghai will experience even greater excitement, proving the Relief Association's hard work worthwhile.

Taihu Bandit Leader Tian Kuaizi Executed by Firing Squad 46

Shanghai Garrison Headquarters Announcement, Law No. 54: For Announcement Purposes

An investigation reveals that Taihu bandit leader Tian Kuaizi (also known as Tian Zhongde), has been apprehended by the Detective Team. He confessed to leading a gang of over a thousand bandits armed with six to seven hundred long and short guns, engaging in rampant robbery in the Taihu area. Therefore, in accordance with Article 1, Section 9 of the Provisional Regulations for the Punishment of Bandits, he shall be sentenced to death. After verifying his identity, he will be bound and escorted to the execution ground for execution by firing squad. This announcement is hereby made for public knowledge.

Details of the execution: Bandit leader Tian Kuaizi (also known as Tian Zhongde), age 40, from Guangzhou, Henan Province, executed on June 27th, 19th year of the Republic of China. (Signed) Commander Xiong Shihui.

Zhang Jinshi Trafficking in People 47

Hu Liangen and Du Axing Escape the Fire Pit

An old woman named Zhang Jinshi, residing at Huoban Lane, Hangzhou City Station, is a matchmaker of sorts. Each year, she travels between Shanghai and Hangzhou, claiming to find employment for impoverished women, but in reality, she traffics them into prostitution. Recently, she boasted to her neighbors that she was familiar with Shanghai's famous three major companies and that most of their female escorts were introduced by her, claiming it was highly lucrative. Two young ladies from humble families, Hu Liangen and Du Axing, both around seventeen or eighteen years old, were enticed by her claims and pleaded for her help. Zhang readily agreed, stating that there would be business opportunities in Shanghai and instructed the two girls to follow her. The girls happily complied, but upon arriving in Shanghai, no company or escort positions were found. Instead, the two girls were sold to a meat shop on Avenue Edward VII. For only five days, the madam and procurer forced the girls to receive clients every night. The two girls, unable to bear the torment and suffering, used the four dollars they had and fled to the South Railway Station early yesterday morning to purchase tickets to return to Hangzhou. They were about to board the train in twenty minutes when the procurer and Zhang Jinshi discovered their escape and pursued them to the station, intending to force them to return. A patrolling police officer noticed the commotion and intervened. The procurer fled, but Zhang Jinshi was apprehended and taken to the police station for questioning. After clarifying the situation, she was immediately sent to the local court for interrogation by the prosecutor, who ordered her detention. The two girls were sent to the hall to await their families to claim them.

Postponed for Further Hearing

Lawyer Tan Xinzhen, formerly a judge of the Provisional Court, had a chauffeur named Zhang Cheng who, on April 20th, was playing with his master's car on Tianjin Road when he accidentally engaged the gears, causing the car to surge forward and fatally crush two pedestrians, Cai Runsheng and another, and injure four others. Lovelorn Man's Farewell Words 49

Yi Tingzai Rescued After Jumping into the River

Yesterday at half past noon, a young man boarded a ferry from the Ning Shao Wharf at the Sixteenth Bund to Lujiazui. While midstream, the young man attempted to jump into the Huangpu River to commit suicide. Fortunately, a deckhand noticed him and immediately pulled him back, handing him over to the dock police, who took him to the Public Security Bureau, District Three, for questioning. The young man identified himself as Dong Tingzai, nineteen years old, from Haimen, residing at No. 2 Chongde Lane, Zhao's Residence, Puxi. He had been an apprentice at the shop of his master, Ren Yaozan, for two and a half years. Last month, he had fallen deeply in love with a woman surnamed Gu, named Xiaying (seventeen years old), who lived nearby. However, their relationship was discovered by his master's uncle, Ren Yaoshui, who severely reprimanded him and sent a telegram to his master in Nanjing, fearing that he would be dismissed and unable to face his family, so he attempted suicide. Three suicide notes and a poem-like song describing his love affair (lengthy lyrics omitted) were found in his pocket. Director Zhang ordered that his master's uncle, Ren Yaoshui, be summoned to take him back and keep him under supervision.

Letter to his lover, Xiaying: Xiaying, I am now dead, and you must be pleased. I have always treated you as if you were no better than a prostitute, utterly heartless. Though my death is not worth regretting, your reputation is already half-gone. Now that I am dead, you are free to choose whatever you want. However, I am not dying from jealousy but from love. If you pity my suffering, please do not marry within three years or flirt with young men. I would die content. This is something you know in your heart, so I need not bother you further. But even in death, my heart does not die, so I leave these few words. If you obey, my soul will forever bow at your pomegranate skirt. Dong Tingzai's last words.

Letter to his father: Honorable Father, I respectfully report that I have neglected my studies due to infatuation with a woman, and it is entirely my fault. Now that the matter has been exposed, there is no way to remedy it. My master is unwilling to keep me, and I have no face to see you. My life is over, and I cannot repay your kindness in this life. In the next life, I will repay you as an ox or a horse. There is nothing more to say in this letter, so I bid you farewell forever. Please do not grieve, as if you had never had a son. Please always relieve your heart from sorrow. Respectfully, I wish you well. Your son, Dong Tingzai, kneeling in death.

Letter to my friend, Wenjie: My dear brother Wenjie, I bow my head to you. I am writing to apologize for my excessive indulgence in pleasure, which has led to my emotional downfall and burdened you. I am writing to you before my death to say goodbye. I hope you will advise young men to avoid going astray. As the saying goes, "The falling flowers have intentions, but the flowing water is heartless." My heart is extremely troubled. I will not bother you further. We will not meet in this life, but we will meet in the afterlife. With this, I wish you well. Your brother, Dong Tingzai, in his last letter.

Two Copper Coins Take a Life 50

Xu Debiao, a 21-year-old cart puller from Yancheng, borrowed two copper coins from his friend, surnamed Xie, at noon the other day while crossing the Suzhou Creek in front of the Yongyu Textile Factory. Xie only had those coins for his own use. The ferryman, Li Fugui, seeing that Xu had no money, ordered him to disembark. However, it was already late, and Xu was eager to get to the Ban Nan area to take over the cart. Disregarding the danger, Xu jumped into the water and grabbed onto the stern of the boat, pulling it towards the other bank. Li, enraged by this, raised his pole and threatened to strike Xu if he did not let go. Xu had no choice but to release the boat and try to swim to the other side but could not reach it and drowned. He called for help but was rescued by a nearby cargo ship, already lifeless. Xu's wife, Zhou, reported the incident to the water patrol, requesting an investigation. The police have detained Li for investigation.

Drowning While Bathing in Cold Water 51

Zhang Chenglin, son of Zhang Wenxiu from Jiangbei, was eighteen years old. Around 10 AM the other day, he drowned in the Suzhou Creek while bathing due to his lack of swimming skills. His body was discovered yesterday morning in Tanziwan. His father reported the incident to the Public Security Bureau.

Jin Lianghao, a worker at a local electric factory in Duanjia Lane, North Shanghai, was from Wenzhou. After finishing work at the factory the other day, he went to a nearby river to bathe in cold water due to the hot weather. He drowned due to his lack of swimming skills. When factory employees learned of the incident, they rushed to rescue him, but his body had already surfaced. They immediately reported the incident to the police, who in turn reported it to the local court. The court dispatched a prosecutor yesterday to confirm that he had indeed drowned. As he had no family in the area, the factory prepared a coffin for him.

Jian Mu Industry Decides to Raise Prices 54

Effective July 1st

Dozens of companies in the building timber industry in this city have been suffering due to the high sales of imported pine in the country, causing the price of domestically produced building timber to plummet. Due to the scarcity of timber from Fujian and rising import prices, the industry has called a meeting of all members to collectively decide to raise the price of all timber, regardless of size, by two strings of cash above the original price, effective July 1st, to maintain business and protect capital.

Rice Prices Rise, Suspension of Savings for Patrol Officers and Sergeants 56

Instruction from the Municipal Public Safety Bureau

The Municipal Public Safety Bureau issued the following instruction to all district stations and teams yesterday:

"It has come to our attention that the Bureau previously established a savings plan for patrol officers and sergeants to ensure their livelihood and security, allowing them to focus on their duties. With the approval of the Municipal Government, each district station and team was instructed to deduct a portion of their monthly salary and deposit it in a bank to accumulate interest. The Police Savings Regulations were also announced and implemented. However, the price of rice in the city has recently risen to unprecedented levels, significantly increasing the living expenses of these patrol officers and sergeants. To address these concerns, the Director of the Bureau has decided to temporarily suspend the savings plan from July 1st. Salaries will be paid in full, according to the original amount. The relevant department has been instructed to notify the managing bank to verify the amounts of all previous monthly deposits and promptly submit the passbooks to the Bureau for distribution to the respective commanding officers, who will then distribute them to the officers themselves. When rice prices return to normal, the situation will be reassessed, and the savings plan will be resumed. In addition to reporting this to the Mayor, all district station and team leaders are instructed to inform their subordinates to comply with this order." Signed, Director Yuan Liang, June 28th, 19th year of the Republic of China.

Former Qing Official Yu Shou Zhang Kidnapped and Rescued 57

Wang Lansheng Turns Off the Engine

Kidnappers Flee in Panic

Around 8 PM yesterday evening, an incident involving four armed kidnappers occurred on Avenue Mengdelan, targeting Yu Shou Zhang, a former Qing official from Shaoxing, residing at No. 323 Weifeng Lane, Weihaiwei Road, Huxi. The inept kidnappers were unable to drive the car, allowing the hostage to escape. The following is an investigation report by our reporter:

The Hostage's Family: Yu Shou Zhang, also known as Zuotang, is a native of Shaoxing, Zhejiang, and is over forty years old. He is a former Qing official who retired long ago due to the decline of politics and now lives as a recluse in Shanghai. He used his savings from his official career to build a residence at No. 323 Weifeng Lane, Weihaiwei Road, Huxi, and owns a car with license plate number 1084. He lives a quiet life, rarely leaving his home and spending time with his family.

The "Three-Eight" Gathering: At 7:45 PM yesterday, Yu Shou Zhang was attending a "Three-Eight" dinner party, a tradition he started with a few close friends four or five years ago. The dinner is held on the 3rd and 8th days of the month, with each person taking turns to host and provide an opportunity for friends to talk and socialize. Yesterday, Yu's close friend, surnamed Zhang, was the host. Yu changed into a new outfit and instructed his driver, Wang Lansheng, to drive his car directly to Zhang's residence at No. 11 Avenue Mengdelan, intending to meet with Zhang and go to a restaurant for the dinner.

Sudden Kidnapping: After Yu Shou Zhang's car arrived at Zhang's residence, he chatted briefly with a friend before deciding to go out for dinner. He instructed his driver to drive the car out, accompanied by a servant surnamed Xu. As the car exited the lane, four men in short clothing, two of whom were wielding handguns, blocked Yu's path, telling him not to make a sound, or he would be killed. The other two men pointed their guns at the driver, Wang Lansheng, and the servant, Xu, ordering them to stop the engine and get out of the car.

The Driver's Clever Plan: Wang Lansheng, recognizing the danger posed by the armed kidnappers, knew that resistance could be fatal. In a moment of quick thinking, he turned off the engine. Wang Lansheng and the servant, Xu, calmly exited the car and stood by the road. The kidnappers then forced Yu Shou Zhang into the car, holding guns to his waist. Yu was stunned and unable to move. Two other kidnappers sat in the driver's seat, intending to start the engine and drive away at full speed.

Kidnappers Escape: However, the kidnappers were unable to start the car despite repeated attempts. The engine remained stubbornly unresponsive. The driver, Wang Lansheng, saw that the kidnappers were unable to drive the car. To rescue his master, he immediately began blowing the car horn and shouting "Kidnapping!" Hearing the commotion, nearby police officers and detectives rushed to the scene. Seeing that the situation was dire, the kidnappers abandoned their plan to kidnap the "God of Wealth" and fled the scene. Fortunately, no shots were fired, and Yu Shou Zhang escaped unharmed.

Cheng Zhaoqing Passes Away 58

The literary scholar Cheng Zhaoqing passed away at his home in South Shanghai on May 22nd, at the age of 56. In his youth, Mr. Cheng served in prominent positions in Fujian, Xiamen, Yan, and Qi. In his later years, he retired from public life and devoted himself to social work. His sudden passing has been mourned by all who knew him. The funeral will be held today at Haichao Temple.

Jiangwan Epidemic Hospital to Open the Day After Tomorrow 59

The Jiangwan Epidemic Hospital has been in operation for many years, saving countless lives. As the new building has not yet been completed, the hospital will temporarily be located at the Jiangwan Great Temple West Fire Station. The hospital will open on July 1st, with consultation hours from 9 AM to 4 PM daily. Wang Hanli has been appointed as the Director, Zhu Ziyun as the Financial Director, Ye Boyang as the Chief Physician, and Wu Zhenjia as the Assistant Physician.

Acknowledgement: I would like to thank Mr. W.J. Keu, Park Manager of the Public Concession, for generously providing me with two annual passes and two concert tickets. Thank you.

Weather Report 60

The Xujiahui Observatory reported at 4:30 PM yesterday that the Yangtze River basin will experience hot and cloudy weather with thunderstorms. The wind direction over the Yellow Sea and East China Sea is uncertain. The hurricane east of Northern Luzon will gradually turn northwards. There will be severe weather south of Miyako Island and along the coast of Annam.

Yesterday, in the 24 hours prior to 3 PM, the highest temperature in this city was 98.0 degrees and the lowest was 76.8 degrees. On the same day last year, the highest temperature was 77.9 degrees and the lowest was 71.2 degrees.

Temporary Suspension of Summer Military Training for High Schools 61

The Ministry of Education has approved a request from the Training Supervision Department to temporarily postpone the three-week continuous military training for high schools and above, originally scheduled for the summer. In addition to instructing universities and vocational schools, the Ministry has also issued a circular to the education departments and bureaus of all provinces and cities, stating:

"In response to the Training Supervision Department's request, [based on reports from the Ministry's representatives in Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and other provinces, citing various difficulties expressed by the administrators of high schools and above regarding the three-week continuous strict military training stipulated in the military education plan during the summer vacation, we respectfully request that you consider amending the three-week military training to be implemented during the summer vacation of the current year]. As there are indeed obstacles to conducting the training this summer, we agree to temporarily postpone it. In addition to instructing all military instructors to comply, we are also issuing a circular for your review and for distribution to all schools." Therefore, all public and private high schools and higher institutions are instructed to comply with this order.

Ministry of Education Defines Medical Study Procedures 62

The Ministry of Education has defined the medical study procedures and has issued a notice stating: "Medical education is of utmost importance, and the study procedures should be clarified and adhered to. The Ministry has therefore stipulated that students applying to university medical colleges must have completed high school. They must then complete a two-year pre-medical program before entering the five-year undergraduate program. These pre-medical programs will be administered by the university's science college. Independent medical colleges or those facing special circumstances (such as universities without a science college or where the science and medical colleges are far apart) may request that another university's science college administer the pre-medical program. In unavoidable circumstances, the college may establish its own pre-medical program. All university medical colleges and independent medical colleges must comply with these regulations."

to Inspect Zhejiang University and Vocational Schools

Zhu Jingnong, Permanent Secretary of the Ministry of Education, departed from Beijing to inspect the national universities under his jurisdiction. He first arrived in Shanghai at Jiaotong University and then traveled to Hangzhou to inspect
